Over 700,000 Palestinians were [expelled by or fled](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Palestinian_exodus "1948 Palestinian exodus") by [Zionist militias](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zionist_political_violence "Zionist political violence") and the [Israeli military](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces "Israel Defense Forces")—what would become known in Arabic as the _[Nakba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nakba "Nakba")_ ("catastrophe").<sup id="cite_ref-218"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-218">[209]</a></sup> The events also led to the destruction of most of Palestine's predominantly Arab population's society, [culture](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_Palestine "Culture of Palestine"), [identity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_identity "Palestinian identity"), political rights, and [national aspirations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_nationalism "Palestinian nationalism"). Some 156,000 remained and became [Arab citizens of Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_citizens_of_Israel "Arab citizens of Israel").<sup id="cite_ref-:2_38-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-:2-38">[30]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Raising_the_Ink_Flag_at_Umm_Rashrash_(Eilat)_(3x4).jpg)

Raising of the [Ink Flag](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ink_Flag "Ink Flag") on 10 March 1949, marking the end of the [1948 war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War "1948 Arab–Israeli War")

Israel [was admitted](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_273 "United Nations General Assembly Resolution 273") as a member of the UN on 11 May 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-219"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-219">[210]</a></sup> An Israeli-Jordanian attempt at negotiating a peace agreement broke down after the [British government](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_government "British government"), fearful of the Egyptian reaction to such a treaty, expressed their opposition to the [Jordanian government](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_Jordan "Government of Jordan").<sup id="cite_ref-220"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-220">[211]</a></sup> In the early years of the state, the [Labor Zionist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labor_Zionism "Labor Zionism") movement led by Prime Minister [David Ben-Gurion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Ben-Gurion "David Ben-Gurion") dominated [Israeli politics](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_of_Israel "Politics of Israel").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELustick198837–39_221-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTELustick198837%E2%80%9339-221">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-222">[213]</a></sup>

Immigration to Israel during the late 1940s and early 1950s was aided by the Israeli Immigration Department and the non-government sponsored [Mossad LeAliyah Bet](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mossad_LeAliyah_Bet "Mossad LeAliyah Bet") (lit. "Institute for [Immigration B](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah_Bet "Aliyah Bet")").<sup id="cite_ref-223"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-223">[214]</a></sup> The latter engaged in clandestine operations in countries, particularly in the Middle East and Eastern Europe, where the lives of Jews were believed to be in danger and exit was difficult. Mossad LeAliyah Bet was disbanded in 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-224"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-224">[215]</a></sup> The immigration was in accordance with the [One Million Plan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/One_Million_Plan "One Million Plan"). Some immigrants held Zionist beliefs or came for the promise of a better life, while others moved to escape persecution or were expelled.<sup id="cite_ref-225"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-225">[216]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-226">[217]</a></sup>

An [influx of Holocaust survivors](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah#Early_statehood_(1948%E2%80%931960) "Aliyah") and [Jews from Arab and Muslim countries](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_Arab_and_Muslim_countries "Jewish exodus from Arab and Muslim countries") to Israel during the first three years increased the number of Jews from 700,000 to 1,400,000. By 1958, the population had risen to two million.<sup id="cite_ref-227"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-227">[218]</a></sup> Between 1948 and 1970, approximately 1,150,000 Jewish refugees relocated to Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-228"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-228">[219]</a></sup> Some new immigrants arrived as refugees and were housed in temporary camps known as _[ma'abarot](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma%27abarot "Ma'abarot")_; by 1952, over 200,000 people were living in these tent cities.<sup id="cite_ref-229"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-229">[220]</a></sup> [Jews of European background](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews "Ashkenazi Jews") were often treated more favorably than Jews from [Middle Eastern](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mizrahi_Jews "Mizrahi Jews") and [North African](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sephardi_Jews "Sephardi Jews") countries—housing units reserved for the latter were often re-designated for the former, so Jews newly arrived from Arab lands generally ended up staying longer in transit camps.<sup id="cite_ref-230"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-230">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev2007155–157_231-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev2007155%E2%80%93157-231">[222]</a></sup> During this period, food, clothes and furniture were rationed in what became known as the [austerity period](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austerity_in_Israel "Austerity in Israel"). The need to solve the crisis led Ben-Gurion to sign a [reparations agreement with West Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reparations_Agreement_between_Israel_and_West_Germany "Reparations Agreement between Israel and West Germany") that triggered mass protests by Jews angered at the idea that Israel could accept monetary compensation for the Holocaust.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShindler200249–50_232-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShindler200249%E2%80%9350-232">[223]</a></sup>

#### Arab–Israeli conflict

During the 1950s, Israel was frequently [attacked](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_attacks_against_Israeli_civilians_before_1967 "List of attacks against Israeli civilians before 1967") by [Palestinian fedayeen](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_fedayeen "Palestinian fedayeen"), nearly always against civilians,<sup id="cite_ref-233"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-233">[224]</a></sup> mainly from the Egyptian-occupied Gaza Strip,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGilbert200558_234-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert200558-234">[225]</a></sup> leading to several Israeli [reprisal operations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reprisal_operations "Reprisal operations"). In 1956, the UK and France aimed at regaining control of the [Suez Canal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Canal "Suez Canal"), which Egypt had nationalized. The continued blockade of the Suez Canal and [Straits of Tiran](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Straits_of_Tiran "Straits of Tiran") to Israeli shipping, together with increasing Fedayeen attacks against Israel's southern population and recent Arab threatening statements, prompted Israel to attack Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-235"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-235">[226]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-236">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-237">[228]</a></sup> Israel joined [a secret alliance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protocol_of_S%C3%A8vres "Protocol of Sèvres") with the UK and France and overran the [Sinai Peninsula](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula "Sinai Peninsula") in the [Suez Crisis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suez_Crisis "Suez Crisis"), but was pressured to withdraw by the UN in return for guarantees of Israeli shipping rights.<sup id="cite_ref-238"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-238">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-239">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-240">[231]</a></sup> The war resulted in significant reduction of Israeli border infiltration.<sup id="cite_ref-241"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-241">[232]</a></sup>

[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1961-04-13_Tale_Of_Century_-_Eichmann_Tried_For_War_Crimes.ogv "Play video")Duration: 1 minute and 14 seconds.Subtitles available.[](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1961-04-13_Tale_Of_Century_-_Eichmann_Tried_For_War_Crimes.ogv)

U.S. newsreel on the trial of [Adolf Eichmann](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann "Adolf Eichmann")

In the early 1960s, Israel captured Nazi war criminal [Adolf Eichmann](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann "Adolf Eichmann") in Argentina and brought him to Israel for [trial](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eichmann_trial "Eichmann trial").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBascomb2009219–229_242-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBascomb2009219%E2%80%93229-242">[233]</a></sup> Eichmann remains the only person executed in Israel by conviction in an [Israeli civilian court](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_judicial_system "Israeli judicial system").<sup id="cite_ref-243"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-243">[234]</a></sup> During the spring and summer of 1963 Israel was engaged in a diplomatic standoff with the United States due to the Israeli [nuclear programme](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_Israel "Nuclear weapons and Israel").<sup id="cite_ref-Haaretz2019_244-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Haaretz2019-244">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-245">[236]</a></sup>

Since 1964, Arab countries, concerned over Israeli plans to divert waters of the [Jordan River](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_River "Jordan River") into the [coastal plain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_coastal_plain "Israeli coastal plain"),<sup id="cite_ref-246"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-246">[237]</a></sup> had been trying to divert the headwaters to deprive Israel of water resources, provoking [tensions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_over_Water_(Jordan_river) "War over Water (Jordan river)") between Israel on the one hand, and Syria and Lebanon on the other. [Arab nationalists](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_nationalist "Arab nationalist") led by Egyptian President [Gamal Abdel Nasser](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser "Gamal Abdel Nasser") refused to recognize Israel and called for its destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-RoutledgeAtlas_247-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-RoutledgeAtlas-247">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-248">[239]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-249">[240]</a></sup> By 1966, Israeli-Arab relations had deteriorated to the point of battles taking place between Israeli and Arab forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev2007178_250-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev2007178-250">[241]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Six_Day_War_Territories.svg)

Territory held by Israel:

  after the war

The [Sinai Peninsula](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula "Sinai Peninsula") was returned to Egypt in 1982.

In May 1967, Egypt massed its army near the border with Israel, expelled [UN peacekeepers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Emergency_Force "United Nations Emergency Force"), stationed in the Sinai Peninsula since 1957, and blocked Israel's access to the Red Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-251"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-251">[242]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-252"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-252">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-253">[244]</a></sup> Other Arab states mobilized their forces.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegev2007289_254-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegev2007289-254">[245]</a></sup> Israel reiterated that these actions were a _[casus belli](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Casus_belli "Casus belli")_ and launched a [pre-emptive strike](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Focus "Operation Focus") against Egypt in June. Jordan, Syria and Iraq attacked Israel. In the [Six-Day War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six-Day_War "Six-Day War"), Israel captured and occupied the West Bank from Jordan, the Gaza Strip and Sinai Peninsula from Egypt, and the [Golan Heights](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golan_Heights "Golan Heights") from Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-255"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-255">[246]</a></sup> Jerusalem's boundaries were enlarged, incorporating [East Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Jerusalem "East Jerusalem"). The 1949 [Green Line](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Line_(Israel) "Green Line (Israel)") became the administrative boundary between Israel and the [occupied territories](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories "Israeli-occupied territories").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShlayRosen2010362–363_256-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShlayRosen2010362%E2%80%93363-256">[247]</a></sup>

Following the 1967 war and the "[Three Nos](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three_Nos "Three Nos")" resolution of the Arab League, Israel faced attacks from the Egyptians in the Sinai Peninsula during the 1967–1970 [War of Attrition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_Attrition "War of Attrition"), and from Palestinian groups targeting Israelis in the occupied territories, globally, and in Israel. Most important among the Palestinian and Arab groups was the [Palestinian Liberation Organization](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_Liberation_Organization "Palestinian Liberation Organization") (PLO), established in 1964, which initially committed itself to "armed struggle as the only way to liberate the homeland".<sup id="cite_ref-257"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-257">[248]</a></sup> In the late 1960s and early 1970s, Palestinian groups launched [attacks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_political_violence "Palestinian political violence")<sup id="cite_ref-258"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-258">[249]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-259">[250]</a></sup> against Israeli and Jewish targets around the world,<sup id="cite_ref-260"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-260">[251]</a></sup> including [a massacre of Israeli athletes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munich_massacre "Munich massacre") at the [1972 Summer Olympics](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics "1972 Summer Olympics") in Munich. The Israeli government responded with an [assassination campaign](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Wrath_of_God "Operation Wrath of God") against the organizers of the massacre, a [bombing](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_Israeli_air_raid_in_Syria_and_Lebanon "1972 Israeli air raid in Syria and Lebanon") and a [raid on the PLO headquarters in Lebanon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_Israeli_raid_on_Lebanon "1973 Israeli raid on Lebanon").

On 6 October 1973, the Egyptian and Syrian armies launched [a surprise attack](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Badr_(1973) "Operation Badr (1973)") against Israeli forces in the Sinai Peninsula and Golan Heights, opening the [Yom Kippur War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War "Yom Kippur War"). The war ended on 25 October with Israel repelling Egyptian and Syrian forces but suffering great losses.<sup id="cite_ref-261"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-261">[252]</a></sup> An [internal inquiry](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agranat_Commission "Agranat Commission") exonerated [the government](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fifteenth_government_of_Israel "Fifteenth government of Israel") of responsibility for failures before and during the war, but public anger forced Prime Minister [Golda Meir](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golda_Meir "Golda Meir") to resign.<sup id="cite_ref-262"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-262">[253]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2023)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In July 1976, an airliner was hijacked in flight from Israel to France by Palestinian guerrillas and landed at [Entebbe International Airport](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entebbe_International_Airport "Entebbe International Airport"), Uganda. Israeli commandos [rescued](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Entebbe "Operation Entebbe") 102 out of 106 Israeli hostages.

#### Peace process

The [1977 Knesset elections](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_Israeli_legislative_election "1977 Israeli legislative election") marked a major turning point in Israeli political history as [Menachem Begin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menachem_Begin "Menachem Begin")'s [Likud](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Likud "Likud") party took control from the [Labor Party](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labor_Party_(Israel) "Labor Party (Israel)").<sup id="cite_ref-263"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-263">[254]</a></sup> Later that year, Egyptian President [Anwar El Sadat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anwar_El_Sadat "Anwar El Sadat") made a trip to Israel and spoke before the [Knesset](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knesset "Knesset") in what was the first recognition of Israel by an Arab head of state.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBregman2002171–174_264-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBregman2002171%E2%80%93174-264">[255]</a></sup> Sadat and Begin signed the [Camp David Accords](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camp_David_Accords "Camp David Accords") (1978) and the [Egypt–Israel peace treaty](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Israel_peace_treaty "Egypt–Israel peace treaty") (1979).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBregman2002186–187_265-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBregman2002186%E2%80%93187-265">[256]</a></sup> In return, Israel withdrew from the Sinai Peninsula and agreed to enter negotiations over an autonomy for Palestinians in the West Bank and the Gaza Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBregman2002186–187_265-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBregman2002186%E2%80%93187-265">[256]</a></sup>

On 11 March 1978, a PLO guerilla raid from Lebanon led to the [Coastal Road massacre](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coastal_Road_massacre "Coastal Road massacre"). Israel responded by launching an [invasion of southern Lebanon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978_South_Lebanon_conflict "1978 South Lebanon conflict") to destroy PLO bases. Most PLO fighters withdrew, but Israel was able to secure southern Lebanon until a [UN force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Force_in_Lebanon "United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon") and the Lebanese army could take over. The PLO soon resumed its [insurgency](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_insurgency_in_South_Lebanon "Palestinian insurgency in South Lebanon") against Israel. In the next few years, the PLO infiltrated the south and kept up a sporadic shelling across the border. Israel carried out numerous retaliatory attacks.

Meanwhile, Begin's government provided incentives for Israelis to [settle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_settlements "Israeli settlements") in the [occupied West Bank](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_the_West_Bank "Israeli occupation of the West Bank"), increasing friction with the Palestinians there.<sup id="cite_ref-266"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-266">[257]</a></sup> The [Jerusalem Law](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem_Law "Jerusalem Law") (1980) was believed by some to reaffirm Israel's 1967 annexation of Jerusalem by government decree, and [reignited international controversy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/UN_Security_Council_Resolution_478 "UN Security Council Resolution 478") over the [status of the city](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Positions_on_Jerusalem "Positions on Jerusalem"). No Israeli legislation has defined the territory of Israel and no act specifically included East Jerusalem therein.<sup id="cite_ref-267"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-267">[258]</a></sup> In 1981 Israel [effectively annexed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golan_Heights_Law "Golan Heights Law") the [Golan Heights](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golan_Heights "Golan Heights").<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_golan_profile_268-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-bbc_golan_profile-268">[259]</a></sup> The international community largely rejected these moves, with the UN Security Council declaring both the Jerusalem Law and the Golan Heights Law null and void.<sup id="cite_ref-269"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-269">[260]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-270">[261]</a></sup> Several waves of [Ethiopian Jews](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethiopian_Jews "Ethiopian Jews") [immigrated](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliyah_from_Ethiopia "Aliyah from Ethiopia") to Israel since the 1980s, while between 1990 and 1994, [immigration from the post-Soviet states](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990s_Post-Soviet_aliyah "1990s Post-Soviet aliyah") increased Israel's population by twelve percent.<sup id="cite_ref-271"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-271">[262]</a></sup>

On 7 June 1981, during the [Iran–Iraq War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War "Iran–Iraq War"), the Israeli air force [destroyed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Opera "Operation Opera") Iraq's sole [nuclear reactor](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osirak "Osirak") under construction just outside [Baghdad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad"), to impede Iraq's nuclear weapons programme. Following a series of PLO attacks in 1982, Israel [invaded](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_Lebanon_War "1982 Lebanon War") Lebanon to destroy the PLO bases.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBregman2002199_272-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBregman2002199-272">[263]</a></sup> In the first six days, the Israelis destroyed the military forces of the PLO in Lebanon and decisively defeated the Syrians. An Israeli government inquiry (the [Kahan Commission](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kahan_Commission "Kahan Commission")) held Begin and several Israeli generals indirectly responsible for the [Sabra and Shatila massacre](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabra_and_Shatila_massacre "Sabra and Shatila massacre") and held [Defense minister](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defense_Minister_of_Israel "Defense Minister of Israel") [Ariel Sharon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ariel_Sharon "Ariel Sharon") as bearing "personal responsibility".<sup id="cite_ref-273"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-273">[264]</a></sup> Sharon was forced to resign.<sup id="cite_ref-274"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-274">[265]</a></sup> In 1985, Israel responded to a Palestinian [terrorist attack](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larnaca_yacht_killings "Larnaca yacht killings") in [Cyprus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus") by [bombing](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Wooden_Leg "Operation Wooden Leg") the PLO headquarters in Tunisia. Israel withdrew from most of Lebanon in 1986, but maintained a [borderland buffer zone](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_Southern_Lebanon "Israeli occupation of Southern Lebanon") in southern Lebanon until 2000, from where Israeli forces [engaged in conflict](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Lebanon_conflict_(1985%E2%80%932000) "South Lebanon conflict (1985–2000)") with [Hezbollah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezbollah "Hezbollah"). The [First Intifada](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Intifada "First Intifada"), a Palestinian uprising against Israeli rule,<sup id="cite_ref-275"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-275">[266]</a></sup> broke out in 1987, with waves of uncoordinated demonstrations and violence in the occupied West Bank and Gaza. Over the following six years, the Intifada became more organized and included economic and cultural measures aimed at disrupting the Israeli occupation. Over a thousand people were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-276"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-276">[267]</a></sup> During the 1991 [Gulf War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War "Gulf War"), the PLO supported [Saddam Hussein](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein "Saddam Hussein") and Iraqi missile [attacks against Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_rocket_attacks_on_Israel "Iraqi rocket attacks on Israel"). Despite public outrage, Israel heeded American calls to refrain from hitting back.<sup id="cite_ref-277"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-277">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMowlanaGerbnerSchiller1992111_278-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMowlanaGerbnerSchiller1992111-278">[269]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Government_Press_Office_(GPO)_-_Foreign_Min._Peres_and_King_Hussein.jpg)

[Shimon Peres](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shimon_Peres "Shimon Peres") (left) with [Yitzhak Rabin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin "Yitzhak Rabin") (center) and King [Hussein of Jordan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_of_Jordan "Hussein of Jordan") (right), prior to signing the [Israel–Jordan peace treaty](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Jordan_peace_treaty "Israel–Jordan peace treaty") in 1994

In 1992, [Yitzhak Rabin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin "Yitzhak Rabin") became prime minister following [an election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992_Israeli_legislative_election "1992 Israeli legislative election") in which his party called for compromise with Israel's neighbours.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBregman2002236_279-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBregman2002236-279">[270]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-280">[271]</a></sup> The following year, [Shimon Peres](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shimon_Peres "Shimon Peres") on behalf of Israel, and [Mahmoud Abbas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas "Mahmoud Abbas") for the PLO, signed the [Oslo Accords](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oslo_Accords "Oslo Accords"), which gave the [Palestinian National Authority](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority "Palestinian National Authority") (PNA) the right to govern [parts of the West Bank](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank_Areas_in_the_Oslo_II_Accord "West Bank Areas in the Oslo II Accord") and the Gaza Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-281"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-281">[272]</a></sup> The PLO also [recognized](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Palestine_Liberation_Organization_letters_of_recognition "Israel–Palestine Liberation Organization letters of recognition") Israel's right to exist and pledged an end to terrorism.<sup id="cite_ref-282"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-282">[273]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (January 2023)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1994, the [Israel–Jordan peace treaty](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Jordan_peace_treaty "Israel–Jordan peace treaty") was signed, making Jordan the second Arab country to normalize relations with Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-283"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-283">[274]</a></sup> Arab public support for the Accords was damaged by the continuation of Israeli settlements<sup id="cite_ref-284"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-284">[275]</a></sup> and [checkpoints](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_checkpoint "Israeli checkpoint"), and the deterioration of economic conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-285">[276]</a></sup> Israeli public support for the Accords waned after [Palestinian suicide attacks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_suicide_attacks "List of Palestinian suicide attacks").<sup id="cite_ref-286"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-286">[277]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2024)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (May 2024)">dubious</span></a> <span>– <a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:Israel#Dubious" title="Talk:Israel">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> In November 1995, Yitzhak Rabin [was assassinated](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Yitzhak_Rabin "Assassination of Yitzhak Rabin") by [Yigal Amir](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yigal_Amir "Yigal Amir"), a far-right Jew who opposed the Accords.<sup id="cite_ref-287"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-287">[278]</a></sup>

During [Benjamin Netanyahu's](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu "Benjamin Netanyahu") premiership at the end of the 1990s, Israel agreed to [withdraw](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protocol_Concerning_the_Redeployment_in_Hebron "Protocol Concerning the Redeployment in Hebron") from [Hebron](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebron "Hebron"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBregman2002257_288-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBregman2002257-288">[279]</a></sup> though this was never ratified or implemented,<sup id="cite_ref-289"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-289">[280]</a></sup> and signed the [Wye River Memorandum](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wye_River_Memorandum "Wye River Memorandum"), giving greater control to the PNA.<sup id="cite_ref-290"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-290">[281]</a></sup> [Ehud Barak](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ehud_Barak "Ehud Barak"), [elected](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_Israeli_general_election "1999 Israeli general election") Prime Minister in 1999, withdrew forces from Southern Lebanon and conducted negotiations with PNA Chairman [Yasser Arafat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yasser_Arafat "Yasser Arafat") and U.S. President [Bill Clinton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton "Bill Clinton") at the [2000 Camp David Summit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_Camp_David_Summit "2000 Camp David Summit"). Barak offered a plan for the establishment of a [Palestinian state](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_state "Palestinian state"), including the entirety of the Gaza Strip and over 90% of the West Bank with Jerusalem as a shared capital.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGelvin2005240_291-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGelvin2005240-291">[282]</a></sup> Each side blamed the other for the failure of the talks.

#### 21st century

Learn more

This section needs to be **updated**. The reason given is: the events of the last two decades outside of conflict is barely covered. _(March 2023)_

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rocket_Attacks_fired_at_Israel_from_the_Gaza_Strip_by_year.png)

[Rocket attacks fired at Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel "Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel") from the Gaza Strip, 2001–2021<sup id="cite_ref-pinfold_292-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-pinfold-292">[283]</a></sup>

In late 2000, after a controversial visit by Likud leader [Ariel Sharon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ariel_Sharon "Ariel Sharon") to the [Temple Mount](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Mount "Temple Mount"), the [Second Intifada](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Intifada "Second Intifada") began and continued for the next 4.5 years. [Suicide bombings](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_suicide_attacks "Palestinian suicide attacks") were a recurrent feature of the Intifada.<sup id="cite_ref-293"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-293">[284]</a></sup> Some commentators contend that the Intifada was pre-planned by Arafat due to the collapse of peace talks.<sup id="cite_ref-294"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-294">[285]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-295">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jewishweek_296-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-jewishweek-296">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-atlantic_297-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-atlantic-297">[288]</a></sup> Sharon became prime minister in a [2001 election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001_Israeli_prime_ministerial_election "2001 Israeli prime ministerial election"); he carried out his plan to [unilaterally withdraw](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_disengagement_from_Gaza "Israeli disengagement from Gaza") from the Gaza Strip and spearheaded the construction of the [Israeli West Bank barrier](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier "Israeli West Bank barrier"),<sup id="cite_ref-298"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-298">[289]</a></sup> ending the Intifada.<sup id="cite_ref-299"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-299">[290]</a></sup> Between 2000 and 2008, 1,063 Israelis, 5,517 Palestinians and 64 foreign citizens had been killed.<sup id="cite_ref-300"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-300">[291]</a></sup>

In 2006, a Hezbollah artillery assault on Israel's northern border communities and a [cross-border abduction](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_Hezbollah_cross-border_raid "2006 Hezbollah cross-border raid") of two Israeli soldiers precipitated the month-long [Second Lebanon War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Lebanon_War "Second Lebanon War").<sup id="cite_ref-UN1701_301-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-UN1701-301">[292]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRTZ_Harel_302-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-HRTZ_Harel-302">[293]</a></sup> In 2007, the Israeli Air Force [destroyed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Outside_the_Box "Operation Outside the Box") a nuclear reactor in Syria. In 2008, [a ceasefire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Israel%E2%80%93Hamas_ceasefire "2008 Israel–Hamas ceasefire") between [Hamas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas "Hamas") and Israel collapsed. The [2008–2009 Gaza War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%932009) "Gaza War (2008–2009)") lasted three weeks and ended after Israel announced a unilateral ceasefire.<sup id="cite_ref-303"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-303">[294]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ravid_304-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-ravid-304">[295]</a></sup> Hamas announced its own ceasefire, with its own conditions of complete withdrawal and opening of [border crossings](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip "Blockade of the Gaza Strip"). Despite neither the [rocket launchings](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel "Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel") nor Israeli [retaliatory strikes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_operations_of_the_Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict "Military operations of the Israeli–Palestinian conflict") having completely stopped, the fragile ceasefire remained.<sup id="cite_ref-305"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-305">[296]</a></sup> In what Israel described as a response to [over a hundred Palestinian rocket attacks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel_in_2012 "List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel in 2012") on southern Israeli cities,<sup id="cite_ref-pound_306-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-pound-306">[297]</a></sup> Israel began [an operation in the Gaza Strip](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Israeli_operation_in_the_Gaza_Strip "2012 Israeli operation in the Gaza Strip") in 2012, lasting eight days.<sup id="cite_ref-307"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-307">[298]</a></sup> Israel started another [operation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Gaza_War "2014 Gaza War") in Gaza following an [escalation of rocket attacks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel_in_2014 "List of Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel in 2014") by Hamas in July 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-308"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-308">[299]</a></sup> In May 2021, another [round of fighting](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Israel%E2%80%93Palestine_crisis "2021 Israel–Palestine crisis") took place in Gaza and Israel, lasting eleven days.<sup id="cite_ref-309"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-309">[300]</a></sup>

By the 2010s, [increasing regional cooperation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_alliance "Arab–Israeli alliance") between Israel and [Arab League](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League") countries have been established, culminating in the signing of the [Abraham Accords](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Accords "Abraham Accords"). The Israeli security situation shifted from the traditional [Arab–Israeli conflict](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict "Arab–Israeli conflict") towards the [Iran–Israel proxy conflict](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_proxy_conflict "Iran–Israel proxy conflict") and [direct confrontation with Iran during the Syrian civil war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Israel_conflict_during_the_Syrian_civil_war "Iran–Israel conflict during the Syrian civil war"). On 7 October 2023, Palestinian militant groups from Gaza, led by [Hamas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamas "Hamas"), launched [a series of coordinated attacks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_Hamas_attack_on_Israel "2023 Hamas attack on Israel") on Israel, leading to the start of the [Israel–Hamas war](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Hamas_war "Israel–Hamas war").<sup id="cite_ref-310"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-310">[301]</a></sup> On that day, approximately 1300 Israelis, predominantly civilians, were killed in communities near the Gaza Strip border and [during a music festival](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Re%27im_music_festival_massacre "Re'im music festival massacre"). [Over 200 hostages](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kidnappings_during_the_2023_Israel%E2%80%93Hamas_war "Kidnappings during the 2023 Israel–Hamas war"), including elders, women, and children as young as 9 months, were kidnapped and taken to the Gaza Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-Gillett_311-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Gillett-311">[302]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-312"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-312">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-natureparty_313-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-natureparty-313">[304]</a></sup>

## Geography

-   [v](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template:Israel_Geographical_Map "Template:Israel Geographical Map")
-   [t](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template_talk:Israel_Geographical_Map "Template talk:Israel Geographical Map")
-   [e](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:Israel_Geographical_Map "Special:EditPage/Template:Israel Geographical Map")

Israel is located in the [Levant](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levant "Levant") area of the [Fertile Crescent](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fertile_Crescent "Fertile Crescent"). The country is at the [eastern end](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean "Eastern Mediterranean") of the [Mediterranean Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea "Mediterranean Sea"), bounded by Lebanon to the north, Syria to the northeast, Jordan and the West Bank to the east, and Egypt and the Gaza Strip to the southwest. It lies between latitudes [29°](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/29th_parallel_north "29th parallel north") and [34° N](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/34th_parallel_north "34th parallel north"), and longitudes [34°](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/34th_meridian_east "34th meridian east") and [36° E](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/36th_meridian_east "36th meridian east").

The sovereign territory of Israel (according to the demarcation lines of the [1949 Armistice Agreements](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements "1949 Armistice Agreements") and excluding all territories captured by Israel during the 1967 [Six-Day War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six-Day_War "Six-Day War")) is approximately 20,770 square kilometers (8,019 sq mi), of which two percent is water.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_314-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cia-314">[305]</a></sup> However Israel is so narrow (100 km at its widest, compared to 400 km from north to south) that the [exclusive economic zone](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone "Exclusive economic zone") in the Mediterranean is double the land area of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-315"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-315">[306]</a></sup> The total area under Israeli law, including [East Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Jerusalem "East Jerusalem") and the [Golan Heights](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golan_Heights "Golan Heights"), is 22,072 square kilometers (8,522 sq mi),<sup id="cite_ref-316"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-316">[307]</a></sup> and the total area under Israeli control, including the military-controlled and partially [Palestinian-governed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority "Palestinian National Authority") territory of the [West Bank](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank "West Bank"), is 27,799 square kilometers (10,733 sq mi).<sup id="cite_ref-loc-geo_317-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-loc-geo-317">[308]</a></sup>

Despite its small size, Israel is home to a variety of geographic features, from the [Negev](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev "Negev") desert in the south to the inland fertile [Jezreel Valley](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jezreel_Valley "Jezreel Valley"), mountain ranges of the [Galilee](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galilee "Galilee"), [Carmel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Carmel "Mount Carmel") and toward the [Golan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golan_Heights "Golan Heights") in the north. The [Israeli coastal plain](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_coastal_plain "Israeli coastal plain") on the shores of the Mediterranean is home to most of the nation's population.<sup id="cite_ref-318"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-318">[309]</a></sup> East of the central highlands lies the [Jordan Rift Valley](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_Rift_Valley "Jordan Rift Valley"), a small part of the 6,500-kilometer (4,039 mi) [Great Rift Valley](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Rift_Valley "Great Rift Valley"). The [Jordan River](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_River "Jordan River") runs along the Jordan Rift Valley, from [Mount Hermon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Hermon "Mount Hermon") through the [Hulah Valley](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hulah_Valley "Hulah Valley") and the [Sea of Galilee](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_of_Galilee "Sea of Galilee") to the [Dead Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dead_Sea "Dead Sea"), the [lowest point](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_points_of_Earth "Extreme points of Earth") on the surface of the Earth.<sup id="cite_ref-319"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-319">[310]</a></sup> Further south is the [Arabah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabah "Arabah"), ending with the [Gulf of Eilat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Aqaba "Gulf of Aqaba"), part of the [Red Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Sea "Red Sea"). [Makhtesh](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Makhtesh "Makhtesh"), or "erosion cirques" are unique to the [Negev](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev "Negev") and the [Sinai Peninsula](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula "Sinai Peninsula"), the largest being the [Makhtesh Ramon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Makhtesh_Ramon "Makhtesh Ramon") at 38 km in length.<sup id="cite_ref-320"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-320">[311]</a></sup> Israel has the largest number of plant species per square meter of the countries in the [Mediterranean Basin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin "Mediterranean Basin").<sup id="cite_ref-rinat_321-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-rinat-321">[312]</a></sup> Israel contains four terrestrial ecoregions: [Eastern Mediterranean conifer-sclerophyllous-broadleaf forests](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean_conifer-sclerophyllous-broadleaf_forests "Eastern Mediterranean conifer-sclerophyllous-broadleaf forests"), [Southern Anatolian montane conifer and deciduous forests](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Anatolian_montane_conifer_and_deciduous_forests "Southern Anatolian montane conifer and deciduous forests"), [Arabian Desert](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Desert "Arabian Desert"), and [Mesopotamian shrub desert](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamian_shrub_desert "Mesopotamian shrub desert").<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_322-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-322">[313]</a></sup>

Forests accounted for 8.5% of the country's area in 2016, up from 2% in 1948, as the result of a large-scale forest planting program by the [Jewish National Fund](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_National_Fund "Jewish National Fund").<sup id="cite_ref-323"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-323">[314]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-324">[315]</a></sup>

### Tectonics and seismicity

The [Jordan Rift Valley](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_Rift_Valley "Jordan Rift Valley") is the result of tectonic movements within the [Dead Sea Transform](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dead_Sea_Transform "Dead Sea Transform") (DSF) fault system. The DSF forms the [transform boundary](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transform_fault "Transform fault") between the [African Plate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_Plate "African Plate") to the west and the [Arabian Plate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Plate "Arabian Plate") to the east. The Golan Heights and all of [Jordan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan "Jordan") are part of the Arabian Plate, while the Galilee, West Bank, Coastal Plain, and Negev along with the Sinai Peninsula are on the African Plate. This tectonic disposition leads to a relatively high [seismic activity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_the_Levant "List of earthquakes in the Levant"). The entire Jordan Valley segment is thought to have ruptured repeatedly, for instance during the last two major [earthquakes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_of_Israel#Seismic_activity "Geography of Israel") along this structure in [749](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/749_Galilee_earthquake "749 Galilee earthquake") and [1033](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1033_Jordan_Rift_Valley_earthquake "1033 Jordan Rift Valley earthquake"). The deficit in [slip](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fault_(geology)#Slip,_heave,_throw "Fault (geology)") that has built up since the 1033 event is sufficient to cause an earthquake of M<sub>w</sub> ~7.4.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferry_325-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Ferry-325">[316]</a></sup>

The most catastrophic known earthquakes occurred in 31 BCE, [363](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galilee_earthquake_of_363 "Galilee earthquake of 363"), 749, and 1033 CE, that is every ca. 400 years on average.<sup id="cite_ref-MarcoAFTAU_326-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-MarcoAFTAU-326">[317]</a></sup> Destructive earthquakes leading to serious loss of life strike about every 80 years.<sup id="cite_ref-IllPreped_327-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-IllPreped-327">[318]</a></sup> While stringent construction regulations are in place and recently built structures are earthquake-safe, as of 2007 many public buildings as well as 50,000 residential buildings did not meet the new standards and were "expected to collapse" if exposed to a strong earthquake.<sup id="cite_ref-IllPreped_327-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-IllPreped-327">[318]</a></sup>

### Climate

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Soil_moisture_and_climate_change.svg)

The projections of the [IPCC Sixth Assessment Report](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPCC_Sixth_Assessment_Report "IPCC Sixth Assessment Report") show clearly the impacts of climate change on Israel even at 2 degrees of warming.

Temperatures in Israel vary widely, especially during the winter. Coastal areas, such as those of [Tel Aviv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv "Tel Aviv") and [Haifa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa"), have a typical [Mediterranean climate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_climate "Mediterranean climate") with cool, rainy winters and long, hot summers. The area of [Beersheba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beersheba "Beersheba") and the Northern Negev have a [semi-arid climate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-arid_climate "Semi-arid climate") with hot summers, cool winters, and fewer rainy days. The Southern Negev and the Arava areas have a [desert climate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert_climate "Desert climate") with very hot, dry summers, and mild winters with few days of rain. The highest temperature in the world outside Africa and North America as of 2021, 54 °C (129 °F), was recorded in 1942 in the [Tirat Zvi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tirat_Zvi "Tirat Zvi") kibbutz in the northern Jordan River valley.<sup id="cite_ref-watzman_328-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-watzman-328">[319]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-329"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-329">[320]</a></sup> Mountainous regions can be windy and cold, and areas at elevation of 750 metres (2,460 ft) or more (same elevation as Jerusalem) usually receive at least one [snowfall](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snow_in_Israel "Snow in Israel") each year.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldreich200385_330-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldreich200385-330">[321]</a></sup> From May to September, rain in Israel is rare.<sup id="cite_ref-331"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-331">[322]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-332"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-332">[323]</a></sup>

There are four different [phytogeographic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phytogeographic "Phytogeographic") regions in Israel, due to the country's location between the temperate and tropical zones. For this reason, the flora and fauna are extremely diverse. There are 2,867 known [species of plants in Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_endemic_flora_of_Israel "List of endemic flora of Israel"). Of these, at least 253 species are [introduced](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_adventive_wild_plants_in_Israel "List of adventive wild plants in Israel") and non-native.<sup id="cite_ref-333"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-333">[324]</a></sup> There are 380 [Israeli nature reserves](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_parks_and_nature_reserves_of_Israel "National parks and nature reserves of Israel").<sup id="cite_ref-334"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-334">[325]</a></sup>

With scarce water resources, Israel has developed various water-saving technologies, including [drip irrigation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drip_irrigation "Drip irrigation").<sup id="cite_ref-335"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-335">[326]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (January 2023)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The considerable sunlight available for [solar energy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_energy "Solar energy") makes [Israel the leading nation in solar energy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_power_in_Israel "Solar power in Israel") use per capita—practically every house uses solar panels for water heating.<sup id="cite_ref-Solar_energy_336-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Solar_energy-336">[327]</a></sup> The Israeli [Ministry of Environmental Protection](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Environmental_Protection_(Israel) "Ministry of Environmental Protection (Israel)") has reported that [climate change](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_Israel "Climate change in Israel") "will have a decisive impact on all areas of life", particularly for vulnerable populations.<sup id="cite_ref-MEP_2020_337-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-MEP_2020-337">[328]</a></sup>

## Government and politics

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PikiWiki_Israel_7260_Knesset-Room.jpg)

The [Knesset](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knesset "Knesset") chamber, home to the Israeli parliament

Israel has a [parliamentary system](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_system "Parliamentary system"), [proportional representation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proportional_representation "Proportional representation") and [universal suffrage](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_suffrage "Universal suffrage"). A member of parliament supported by a parliamentary majority becomes the [prime minister](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Israel "Prime Minister of Israel")—usually this is the chair of the largest party. The prime minister is the [head of government](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_government "Head of government") and of [cabinet](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_Israel "Cabinet of Israel").<sup id="cite_ref-cia2_338-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cia2-338">[329]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-339"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-339">[330]</a></sup> The [president](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_Israel "President of Israel") is [head of state](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_state "Head of state"), with limited and largely ceremonial duties.<sup id="cite_ref-cia2_338-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cia2-338">[329]</a></sup>

Israel is governed by a 120-member parliament, known as the [Knesset](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knesset "Knesset"). Membership of the Knesset is based on proportional representation of [political parties](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Israel "List of political parties in Israel"),<sup id="cite_ref-340"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-340">[331]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2023)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> with a 3.25% electoral threshold, which in practice has resulted in coalition governments. Residents of Israeli settlements in the West Bank are eligible to vote<sup id="cite_ref-341"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-341">[332]</a></sup> and after the [2015 election](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_Israeli_legislative_election "2015 Israeli legislative election"), 10 of the 120 members of the Knesset (8%) were settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-342"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-342">[333]</a></sup> Parliamentary [elections](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elections_in_Israel "Elections in Israel") are scheduled every four years, but unstable coalitions or a [no-confidence vote](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motion_of_no_confidence "Motion of no confidence") can dissolve a government earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_42-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cnn-42">[34]</a></sup> The first Arab-led party was established in 1988<sup id="cite_ref-343"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-343">[334]</a></sup> and as of 2022, Arab-led parties hold about 10% of seats.<sup id="cite_ref-344"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-344">[335]</a></sup> The Basic Law: The Knesset (1958) and its amendments prevent a party list from running for election to the Knesset if its objectives or actions include the "negation of the existence of the State of Israel as the state of the Jewish people".

The [Basic Laws of Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basic_Laws_of_Israel "Basic Laws of Israel") function as an [uncodified constitution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uncodified_constitution "Uncodified constitution"). In its Basic Laws, Israel defines itself as a [Jewish and democratic state](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_and_democratic_state "Jewish and democratic state"), and the [nation-state of exclusively the Jewish people](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basic_Law:_Israel_as_the_Nation-State_of_the_Jewish_People "Basic Law: Israel as the Nation-State of the Jewish People").<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse2008_345-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-freedomhouse2008-345">[336]</a></sup> In 2003, the Knesset began to draft an official [constitution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Israel "Constitution of Israel") based on these laws.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_314-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cia-314">[305]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMazie200634_346-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMazie200634-346">[337]</a></sup>

Israel has no official religion,<sup id="cite_ref-347"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-347">[338]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-348"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-348">[339]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-349"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-349">[340]</a></sup> but the definition of the state as "Jewish and democratic" creates a strong connection with Judaism. On 19 July 2018, the Knesset passed a Basic Law that characterizes the State of Israel as principally a "[Nation State of the Jewish People](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basic_Law:_Israel_as_the_Nation-State_of_the_Jewish_People "Basic Law: Israel as the Nation-State of the Jewish People")", and Hebrew as its official language. The bill ascribes, an undefined, "special status" to the Arabic language.<sup id="cite_ref-350"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-350">[341]</a></sup> The same bill gives Jews a unique right to national self-determination, and views the developing of Jewish settlement in the country as "a national interest", empowering the government to "take steps to encourage, advance and implement this interest."<sup id="cite_ref-351"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-351">[342]</a></sup>

### Legal system

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Israel_Supreme_Court.jpg)

[Supreme Court of Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Israel "Supreme Court of Israel"), Givat Ram, Jerusalem

Israel has a [three-tier court system](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_judicial_system "Israeli judicial system"). At the lowest level are [magistrate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magistrate "Magistrate") courts, situated in most cities across the country. Above them are [district courts](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/District_court "District court"), serving as both [appellate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appeal "Appeal") courts and [courts of first instance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trial_court "Trial court"); they are situated in five of Israel's six [districts](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Districts_of_Israel "Districts of Israel"). The third and highest tier is the [Supreme Court](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Israel "Supreme Court of Israel"), located in Jerusalem; it serves a dual role as the highest court of appeals and the [High Court of Justice](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice_(Israel) "High Court of Justice (Israel)"). In the latter role, the Supreme Court rules as a court of first instance, allowing individuals, both citizens and non-citizens, to petition against the decisions of state authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-352"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-352">[343]</a></sup>

Israel's legal system combines three legal traditions: [English common law](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_law "English law"), [civil law](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system) "Civil law (legal system)"), and [Jewish law](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halakha "Halakha").<sup id="cite_ref-cia_314-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cia-314">[305]</a></sup> It is based on the principle of _[stare decisis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stare_decisis "Stare decisis")_ (precedent) and is an [adversarial system](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adversarial_system "Adversarial system"). Court cases are decided by professional judges with no role for juries.<sup id="cite_ref-judiciary_353-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-judiciary-353">[344]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (January 2023)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> [Marriage](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marriage_in_Israel "Marriage in Israel") and divorce are under the jurisdiction of the religious courts: [Jewish](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beth_din "Beth din"), [Muslim](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia "Sharia"), Druze, and Christian. The election of judges is carried out by a [selection committee](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judicial_Selection_Committee_(Israel) "Judicial Selection Committee (Israel)") chaired by the [justice minister](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Justice_(Israel) "Ministry of Justice (Israel)") (currently [Yariv Levin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yariv_Levin "Yariv Levin")).<sup id="cite_ref-354"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-354">[345]</a></sup> Israel's [Basic Law: Human Dignity and Liberty](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basic_Law:_Human_Dignity_and_Liberty "Basic Law: Human Dignity and Liberty") seeks to defend [human rights and liberties in Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_Israel "Human rights in Israel"). The [United Nations Human Rights Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council "United Nations Human Rights Council") and Israeli human rights organization [Adalah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adalah_(legal_center) "Adalah (legal center)") have highlighted that this law does not in fact contain a general provision for equality and non-discrimination.<sup id="cite_ref-adalah_355-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-adalah-355">[346]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-356"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-356">[347]</a></sup> As a result of "[Enclave law](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enclave_law "Enclave law")", large portions of Israeli [civil law](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system) "Civil law (legal system)") are applied to Israeli settlements and Israeli residents in the occupied territories.<sup id="cite_ref-Ben-NaftaliSfard2018_357-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Ben-NaftaliSfard2018-357">[348]</a></sup>

### Administrative divisions

-   [v](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template:Israel_Labelled_Map "Template:Israel Labelled Map")
-   [t](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Template_talk:Israel_Labelled_Map "Template talk:Israel Labelled Map")
-   [e](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:EditPage/Template:Israel_Labelled_Map "Special:EditPage/Template:Israel Labelled Map")

The State of Israel is divided into six main administrative [districts](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Districts_of_Israel "Districts of Israel"), known as _mehozot_ (Hebrew: מחוזות; singular: _mahoz_) – [Center](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_District_(Israel) "Central District (Israel)"), [Haifa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa_District "Haifa District"), [Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem_District "Jerusalem District"), [North](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_District_(Israel) "Northern District (Israel)"), [South](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_District_(Israel) "Southern District (Israel)"), and [Tel Aviv](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv_District "Tel Aviv District") districts, as well as the [Judea and Samaria Area](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judea_and_Samaria_Area "Judea and Samaria Area") in the [West Bank](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank "West Bank"). All of the Judea and Samaria Area and parts of the Jerusalem and Northern districts are not recognized internationally as part of Israel. Districts are further divided into fifteen sub-districts known as _nafot_ (Hebrew: נפות; singular: _nafa_), which are themselves partitioned into fifty natural regions.<sup id="cite_ref-358"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-358">[349]</a></sup>

| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Jews | Arabs | Total | note |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem_District "Jerusalem District") | [Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem") | 66% | 32% | 1,209,700 | <sup id="ref_jerusalemdistrict"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#endnote_jerusalemdistrict">a</a></sup> |
| [North](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_District_(Israel) "Northern District (Israel)") | [Nof HaGalil](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nof_HaGalil "Nof HaGalil") | [Nazareth](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazareth "Nazareth") | 42% | 54% | 1,513,600 |  |
| [Haifa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa_District "Haifa District") | [Haifa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa "Haifa") | 67% | 25% | 1,092,700 |  |
| [Center](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_District_(Israel) "Central District (Israel)") | [Ramla](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramla "Ramla") | [Rishon LeZion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rishon_LeZion "Rishon LeZion") | 87% | 8% | 2,304,300 |  |

**[^a](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#ref_jerusalemdistrict)** Including 361,700 Arabs and 233,900 Jews in [East Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Jerusalem "East Jerusalem"), as of 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-jerusalem_pop_360-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-jerusalem_pop-360">[351]</a></sup>

**[^b](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#ref_judeaandsamaria)** Israeli citizens only.

### Israeli citizenship law

The two primary pieces of legislation relating to Israeli citizenship are the 1950 [Law of Return](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_Return "Law of Return") and 1952 Citizenship Law. The law of return grants Jews the unrestricted [right to immigrate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jus_soli#Restricted_jus_soli "Jus soli") to Israel and obtain Israeli citizenship. Individuals born within the country receive [birthright citizenship](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jus_sanguinis "Jus sanguinis") if at least one parent is a citizen.<sup id="cite_ref-361"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-361">[352]</a></sup>

Israeli law defines Jewish nationality as distinct from Israeli nationality, and the [Supreme Court of Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Israel "Supreme Court of Israel") has ruled that an Israeli nationality does not exist.<sup id="cite_ref-tekiner_362-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-tekiner-362">[353]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-363"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-363">[354]</a></sup> Israeli law defines a Jewish national as any person practicing Judaism and their descendants.<sup id="cite_ref-tekiner_362-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-tekiner-362">[353]</a></sup> Legislation has defined Israel as the [nation state](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation_state "Nation state") of the Jewish people since 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-364"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-364">[355]</a></sup>

Jerusalem</a></td><td><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, Honduras, Guatemala, Nauru, and the United States</td><td><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> as an <a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corpus_separatum_(Jerusalem)" title="Corpus separatum (Jerusalem)">international city</a> along with East Jerusalem</td><td>Various UN member states and the <a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>; <a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">joint sovereignty</a> also widely supported</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golan_Heights" title="Golan Heights">Golan Heights</a></td><td>United States</td><td><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a></td><td>All UN member states except the United States</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Line_(Israel)" title="Green Line (Israel)">Israel (Green Line border)</a></td><td><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_recognition_of_Israel" title="International recognition of Israel">164 UN member states</a></td><td><a>Israel</a></td><td>164 UN member states</td></tr></tbody></table>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Map_of_Israel,_neighbours_and_occupied_territories.svg)

Map of Israel showing the West Bank, the Gaza Strip, and the Golan Heights

In 1967, as a result of the [Six-Day War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six-Day_War "Six-Day War"), Israel captured and [occupied](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli-occupied_territories "Israeli-occupied territories") the [West Bank](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bank "West Bank"), including [East Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Jerusalem "East Jerusalem"), the [Gaza Strip](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip") and the [Golan Heights](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golan_Heights "Golan Heights"). Israel also captured the [Sinai Peninsula](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinai_Peninsula "Sinai Peninsula"), but returned it to Egypt as part of the 1979 [Egypt–Israel peace treaty](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Israel_peace_treaty "Egypt–Israel peace treaty").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBregman2002186–187_265-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBregman2002186%E2%80%93187-265">[256]</a></sup> Between 1982 and 2000, Israel occupied [part of southern Lebanon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_Southern_Lebanon "Israeli occupation of Southern Lebanon"), in what was known as the [Security Belt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Lebanon_Security_Belt "South Lebanon Security Belt"). Since Israel's capture of these territories, [Israeli settlements](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_settlement "Israeli settlement") and military installations have been built within each of them, except Lebanon.

The [Golan Heights](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golan_Heights_Law "Golan Heights Law") and [East Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem_Law "Jerusalem Law") have been fully incorporated into Israel under Israeli law, but not under international law. Israel has applied civilian law to both areas and granted their inhabitants permanent residency status and the ability to [apply for citizenship](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_nationality_law "Israeli nationality law"). The UN Security Council has declared the annexation of the Golan Heights and East Jerusalem to be "null and void" and continues to view the territories as occupied.<sup id="cite_ref-365"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-365">[356]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-366"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-366">[357]</a></sup> The [status](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Positions_on_Jerusalem "Positions on Jerusalem") of East Jerusalem in any future peace settlement has at times been a difficult issue in [negotiations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_peace_process "Israeli–Palestinian peace process") between Israeli governments and representatives of the Palestinians.

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:West_Bank_Fence_South_Hebron.JPG)

[Israeli West Bank barrier](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier "Israeli West Bank barrier") is a separation barrier built by Israel along the Green Line and inside parts of the West Bank.

The West Bank excluding East Jerusalem is known in Israeli law as the [Judea and Samaria Area](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judea_and_Samaria_Area "Judea and Samaria Area"). The almost 400,000 Israeli settlers residing in the area are considered part of Israel's population, have Knesset representation, are subject to a [large part of Israel's civil and criminal laws](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enclave_law "Enclave law"), and their output is considered part of Israel's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-Sher_367-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Sher-367">[358]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oecd_22-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-oecd-22">[fn 4]</a></sup> The land itself is not considered part of Israel under Israeli law, as Israel has consciously refrained from annexing the territory, without ever relinquishing its legal claim to the land or defining a border.<sup id="cite_ref-Sher_367-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Sher-367">[358]</a></sup> Israeli political opposition to annexation is primarily due to the perceived "demographic threat" of incorporating the West Bank's Palestinian population into Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-Sher_367-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Sher-367">[358]</a></sup> Outside of the Israeli settlements, the West Bank remains under direct Israeli military rule, and Palestinians in the area cannot become Israeli citizens. The international community maintains that Israel does not have sovereignty in the West Bank, and considers Israel's control of the area to be the longest military occupation in modern history.<sup id="cite_ref-occhist_370-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-occhist-370">[361]</a></sup> The West Bank [was occupied and annexed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordanian_annexation_of_the_West_Bank "Jordanian annexation of the West Bank") by Jordan in 1950, following the 1949 Armistice Agreements. Only Britain recognized this annexation and Jordan has since [ceded](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordanian_disengagement_from_the_West_Bank "Jordanian disengagement from the West Bank") its claim to the territory to the PLO. The [population](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Palestinian_territories "Demographics of the Palestinian territories") are mainly [Palestinians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_people "Palestinian people"), including [refugees](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_refugee "Palestinian refugee") of the [1948 Arab–Israeli War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War "1948 Arab–Israeli War").<sup id="cite_ref-371"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-371">[362]</a></sup> From their occupation in 1967 until 1993, the Palestinians living in these territories were under [Israeli military administration](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordinator_of_Government_Activities_in_the_Territories "Coordinator of Government Activities in the Territories").
