Since the [Israel–PLO letters of recognition](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Palestine_Liberation_Organization_letters_of_recognition "Israel–Palestine Liberation Organization letters of recognition"), most of the Palestinian population and [cities](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_cities_administered_by_the_State_of_Palestine "List of cities administered by the State of Palestine") have been under the internal jurisdiction of the [Palestinian Authority](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority "Palestinian National Authority"), and only partial Israeli military control, although Israel has redeployed its [troops](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces "Israel Defense Forces") and reinstated full military administration during periods of unrest. In response to increasing attacks during the [Second Intifada](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Intifada "Second Intifada"), the Israeli government started to construct the Israeli West Bank barrier.<sup id="cite_ref-372"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-372">[363]</a></sup> When completed, approximately 13% of the barrier will be constructed on the [Green Line](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Line_(Israel) "Green Line (Israel)") or in Israel with 87% inside the West Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-373"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-373">[364]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-374"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-374">[365]</a></sup>

Israel's claim of universal suffrage has been questioned due to its blurred territorial boundaries and its simultaneous extension of voting rights to Israeli settlers in the occupied territories and denial of voting rights to their Palestinian neighbours, as well as the alleged [ethnocratic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnocracy "Ethnocracy") nature of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-375"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-375">[366]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-376"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-376">[367]</a></sup>

The Gaza Strip is considered to be a "foreign territory" under Israeli law. Israel and Egypt operate a land, air, and sea [blockade of the Gaza Strip](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip "Blockade of the Gaza Strip"). The Gaza Strip was occupied by Israel after 1967. In 2005, as part of [Israel's unilateral disengagement plan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%27s_unilateral_disengagement_plan "Israel's unilateral disengagement plan"), Israel removed its settlers and forces from the territory but continues to maintain [control](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blockade_of_the_Gaza_Strip "Blockade of the Gaza Strip") of its airspace and waters. The international community, including numerous international humanitarian organizations and UN bodies, consider Gaza to remain occupied.<sup id="cite_ref-377"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-377">[368]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-378"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-378">[369]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-379"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-379">[370]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-380"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-380">[371]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-381"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-381">[372]</a></sup> Following the [2007 Battle of Gaza](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Gaza_(2007) "Battle of Gaza (2007)"), when [Hamas assumed power in the Gaza Strip](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governance_of_the_Gaza_Strip "Governance of the Gaza Strip"),<sup id="cite_ref-gaza_382-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-gaza-382">[373]</a></sup> Israel tightened control of the Gaza crossings along [its border](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Gaza_barrier "Israel–Gaza barrier"), as well as by sea and air, and prevented persons from entering and exiting except for isolated cases it deemed humanitarian.<sup id="cite_ref-gaza_382-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-gaza-382">[373]</a></sup> Gaza has a [border with Egypt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza%E2%80%93Egypt_border "Gaza–Egypt border"), and an agreement between Israel, the EU, and the PA governs how border crossings take place.<sup id="cite_ref-383"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-383">[374]</a></sup> The application of democracy to its Palestinian citizens, and the selective application of Israeli democracy in the Israeli-controlled Palestinian territories, has been criticized.<sup id="cite_ref-Slater2020_384-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Slater2020-384">[375]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-White2012_385-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-White2012-385">[376]</a></sup>

#### International opinion

The [International Court of Justice](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice "International Court of Justice") said, in its [2004 advisory opinion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_law_and_the_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict#Ruling_of_the_ICJ "International law and the Arab–Israeli conflict") on the legality of the construction of the [Israeli West Bank barrier](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_West_Bank_barrier "Israeli West Bank barrier"), that the lands captured by Israel in the Six-Day War, including East Jerusalem, are occupied territory, and found that the construction of the wall within the occupied Palestinian territory to violate international law.<sup id="cite_ref-386"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-386">[377]</a></sup> Most negotiations relating to the territories have been on the basis of [UN Security Council Resolution 242](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_242 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 242"), which emphasizes "the inadmissibility of the acquisition of territory by war", and calls on Israel to withdraw from occupied territories in return for normalization of relations with Arab states ("[Land for peace](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_for_peace "Land for peace")").<sup id="cite_ref-387"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-387">[378]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-388"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-388">[379]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-389"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-389">[380]</a></sup> Israel has been criticized for engaging in systematic and widespread violations of [human rights in the occupied territories](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Israeli-occupied_territories "Human rights in the Israeli-occupied territories"), including the occupation itself,<sup id="cite_ref-390"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-390">[381]</a></sup> and [war crimes](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_crime "War crime") against civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-tny1_391-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-tny1-391">[382]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-392"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-392">[383]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-393"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-393">[384]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-394"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-394">[385]</a></sup> The allegations include violations of international humanitarian law<sup id="cite_ref-395"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-395">[386]</a></sup> by the [UN Human Rights Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council "United Nations Human Rights Council"),<sup id="cite_ref-396"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-396">[387]</a></sup> The [U.S. State Department](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._State_Department "U.S. State Department") has called reports of [abuses of significant human rights of Palestinians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_violations_against_Palestinians_by_Israel "Human rights violations against Palestinians by Israel") 'credible' both within Israel<sup id="cite_ref-397"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-397">[388]</a></sup> and the occupied territories.<sup id="cite_ref-398"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-398">[389]</a></sup> [Amnesty International](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International "Amnesty International") and other NGOs have documented mass arbitrary arrests, torture, unlawful killings, systemic abuses and impunity<sup id="cite_ref-399"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-399">[390]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-400"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-400">[391]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-401"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-401">[392]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-402"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-402">[393]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-403"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-403">[394]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-404"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-404">[395]</a></sup> in tandem with a denial of the right to [Palestinian self-determination](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_self-determination "Palestinian self-determination").<sup id="cite_ref-405"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-405">[396]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-406"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-406">[397]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-407"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-407">[398]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-408"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-408">[399]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-409"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-409">[400]</a></sup> Prime Minister Netanyahu has defended the country's security forces for protecting the innocent from terrorists<sup id="cite_ref-410"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-410">[401]</a></sup> and expressed contempt for what he describes as a lack of concern about the human rights violations committed by "criminal killers".<sup id="cite_ref-411"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-411">[402]</a></sup>

The [international community](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_community "International community") widely regards Israeli settlements in the occupied territories [illegal under international law](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_law_and_Israeli_settlements "International law and Israeli settlements").<sup id="cite_ref-412"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-412">[403]</a></sup> [United Nations Security Council Resolution 2334](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_2334 "United Nations Security Council Resolution 2334") (passed 2016) states that Israel's settlement activity constitutes a "flagrant violation" of [international law](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_law "International law") and demands that Israel stop such activity and fulfill its obligations as an [occupying power](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_occupation#The_occupying_power "Military occupation") under the [Fourth Geneva Convention](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourth_Geneva_Convention "Fourth Geneva Convention").<sup id="cite_ref-toi_413-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-toi-413">[404]</a></sup> A [United Nations special rapporteur](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_special_rapporteur "United Nations special rapporteur") concluded that settlement program was a [war crime](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_crime "War crime") under the [Rome Statute](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome_Statute "Rome Statute"),<sup id="cite_ref-414"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-414">[405]</a></sup> and [Amnesty International](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International "Amnesty International") found that the settlement program constitutes an illegal transfer of civilians into occupied territory and "pillage", which is prohibited by the [Hague Conventions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hague_Conventions_of_1899_and_1907 "Hague Conventions of 1899 and 1907") and [Geneva Conventions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geneva_Conventions "Geneva Conventions") as well as being a war crime under the Rome Statute.<sup id="cite_ref-415"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-415">[406]</a></sup>

#### Apartheid accusations

Israel's treatment of the Palestinians within the occupied territories have drawn widespread [accusations that it is guilty](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_and_apartheid "Israel and apartheid") of [apartheid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime_of_apartheid "Crime of apartheid"), a [crime against humanity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime_against_humanity "Crime against humanity") under the Rome Statute and the [International Convention on the Suppression and Punishment of the Crime of Apartheid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Convention_on_the_Suppression_and_Punishment_of_the_Crime_of_Apartheid "International Convention on the Suppression and Punishment of the Crime of Apartheid").<sup id="cite_ref-416"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-416">[407]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-417"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-417">[408]</a></sup> A 2021 survey of academic experts on the Middle East found an increase from 59% to 65% of these scholars describing Israel as a "one-state reality akin to apartheid".<sup id="cite_ref-418"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-418">[409]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-419"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-419">[410]</a></sup> This claim has been affirmed by the Israeli human rights organizations [Yesh Din](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yesh_Din "Yesh Din") and [B'tselem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%27tselem "B'tselem"), along with other international human rights groups, including [Amnesty International](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International "Amnesty International") and [Human Rights Watch](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch "Human Rights Watch"), with the criticism extending to its treatment of [Palestinians within Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_citizens_of_Israel "Palestinian citizens of Israel").<sup id="cite_ref-420"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-420">[411]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:5_421-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-:5-421">[412]</a></sup> Amnesty's report was criticised by politicians and representatives from Israel and its closest allies such as, the US,<sup id="cite_ref-422"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-422">[413]</a></sup> the UK,<sup id="cite_ref-423"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-423">[414]</a></sup> the [European Commission](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Commission "European Commission"),<sup id="cite_ref-424"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-424">[415]</a></sup> Australia,<sup id="cite_ref-425"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-425">[416]</a></sup> Netherlands<sup id="cite_ref-426"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-426">[417]</a></sup> and Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-427"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-427">[418]</a></sup> while said accusations were welcomed by Palestinians,<sup id="cite_ref-428"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-428">[419]</a></sup> representatives from other states,<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (January 2024)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> and organizations such as the [Arab League](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League").<sup id="cite_ref-429"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-429">[420]</a></sup> In 2022, Michael Lynk, a Canadian law professor [appointed by the U.N. Human Rights Council](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Rapporteur_on_the_occupied_Palestinian_territories "United Nations Special Rapporteur on the occupied Palestinian territories") said that the situation met the legal definition of apartheid.<sup id="cite_ref-430"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-430">[421]</a></sup> Subsequent reports from his successor, [Francesca Albanese](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francesca_Albanese "Francesca Albanese") and from [Permanent United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the Israel Palestine conflict](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_United_Nations_Fact_Finding_Mission_on_the_Israel_Palestine_conflict "Permanent United Nations Fact Finding Mission on the Israel Palestine conflict") chair Navi Pillay echoed the opinion.<sup id="cite_ref-431"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-431">[422]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-432"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-432">[423]</a></sup>

### Foreign relations

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Foreign_relations_of_Israel_(map).png)

  Diplomatic relations

  Diplomatic relations suspended

  Former diplomatic relations

  No diplomatic relations, but former trade relations

  No diplomatic relations

Israel maintains diplomatic relations with 164 [UN member states](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations_member_states "United Nations member states"), as well as with the [Holy See](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_See "Holy See"), [Kosovo](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo "Kosovo"), the [Cook Islands](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cook_Islands "Cook Islands") and [Niue](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niue "Niue"). It has 107 [diplomatic missions](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Israel "List of diplomatic missions of Israel");<sup id="cite_ref-433"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-433">[424]</a></sup> countries with whom they have no diplomatic relations include most Muslim countries.<sup id="cite_ref-434"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-434">[425]</a></sup> Six out of twenty-two nations in the [Arab League](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League") have normalized relations with Israel. Israel remains formally in a [state of war with Syria](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Syria_relations "Israel–Syria relations"), a status that dates back uninterrupted to 1948. It has been in a similarly [formal state of war with Lebanon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Lebanon_relations "Israel–Lebanon relations") since the end of the [Lebanese Civil War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War "Lebanese Civil War") in 2000, with the Israel–Lebanon border remaining unagreed by treaty.

Despite the peace treaty between Israel and Egypt, Israel is still widely considered an enemy country among Egyptians.<sup id="cite_ref-435"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-435">[426]</a></sup> Iran withdrew its recognition of Israel during the [Islamic Revolution](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Revolution "Islamic Revolution").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbadi200447–49_436-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbadi200447%E2%80%9349-436">[427]</a></sup> Israeli citizens may not visit Syria, Lebanon, Iraq, Saudi Arabia, and Yemen without permission from the [Ministry of the Interior](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_(Israel) "Ministry of Interior (Israel)").<sup id="cite_ref-437"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-437">[428]</a></sup> As a result of the [2008–09 Gaza War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309) "Gaza War (2008–09)"), Mauritania, Qatar, Bolivia, and Venezuela suspended political and economic ties with Israel,<sup id="cite_ref-al-jaz-eng_438-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-al-jaz-eng-438">[429]</a></sup> though Bolivia renewed ties in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-439"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-439">[430]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton,_Yitzhak_Rabin,_Yasser_Arafat_at_the_White_House_1993-09-13.jpg)

Yitzhak Rabin and Yasser Arafat at the signing ceremony of the [Oslo Accords](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oslo_Accords "Oslo Accords") with then US President [Bill Clinton](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Clinton "Bill Clinton")

The [United States](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Israel–United States relations") and the [Soviet Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Russia_relations "Israel–Russia relations") were the first two countries to recognize the State of Israel, having declared recognition roughly simultaneously.<sup id="cite_ref-440"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-440">[431]</a></sup> Diplomatic relations with the Soviet Union were broken in 1967, following the [Six-Day War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six-Day_War "Six-Day War"), and renewed in October 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-441"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-441">[432]</a></sup> The United States regards Israel as its "most reliable partner in the Middle East",<sup id="cite_ref-442"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-442">[433]</a></sup> based on "common democratic values, religious affinities, and security interests".<sup id="cite_ref-443"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-443">[434]</a></sup> The US has provided $68 billion in [military assistance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_military_relations "Israel–United States military relations") and $32 billion in grants to Israel since 1967, under the [Foreign Assistance Act](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_Assistance_Act "Foreign Assistance Act") (period beginning 1962),<sup id="cite_ref-PNADR900_444-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-PNADR900-444">[435]</a></sup> more than any other country for that period until 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-PNADR900_444-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-PNADR900-444">[435]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-445"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-445">[436]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-446"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-446">[437]</a></sup> Most surveyed Americans have also held consistently favorable views of Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-447"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-447">[438]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-448"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-448">[439]</a></sup> The United Kingdom is seen as having a "natural" [relationship](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations "Israel–United Kingdom relations") with Israel because of the Mandate for Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-449"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-449">[440]</a></sup> By 2007, [Germany](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany%E2%80%93Israel_relations "Germany–Israel relations") had paid 25 billion euros in [reparations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reparations_Agreement_between_Israel_and_West_Germany "Reparations Agreement between Israel and West Germany") to the Israeli state and individual Israeli Holocaust survivors.<sup id="cite_ref-450"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-450">[441]</a></sup> Israel is [included](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93European_Union_relations "Israel–European Union relations") in the European Union's [European Neighbourhood Policy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy "European Neighbourhood Policy").<sup id="cite_ref-451"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-451">[442]</a></sup>

Although Turkey and Israel did not establish full diplomatic relations until 1991,<sup id="cite_ref-452"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-452">[443]</a></sup> Turkey has [cooperated](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93Turkey_relations "Israel–Turkey relations") with the Jewish state since its recognition of Israel in 1949. Turkey's ties to other Muslim-majority nations in the region have at times resulted in pressure from Arab and Muslim states to temper its relationship with Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbadi20044–6_453-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbadi20044%E2%80%936-453">[444]</a></sup> Relations between Turkey and Israel took a downturn after the 2008–09 Gaza War and Israel's [raid of the Gaza flotilla](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_flotilla_raid "Gaza flotilla raid").<sup id="cite_ref-454"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-454">[445]</a></sup> [Relations between Greece and Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greece%E2%80%93Israel_relations "Greece–Israel relations") have improved since 1995 due to the decline of Israeli–Turkish relations.<sup id="cite_ref-455"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-455">[446]</a></sup> The two countries have a defense cooperation agreement and in 2010, the [Israeli Air Force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force "Israeli Air Force") hosted Greece's [Hellenic Air Force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenic_Air_Force "Hellenic Air Force") in a joint exercise. The joint Cyprus-Israel oil and gas explorations centered on the [Leviathan gas field](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leviathan_gas_field "Leviathan gas field") are an important factor for Greece, given its [strong links](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus%E2%80%93Greece_relations "Cyprus–Greece relations") with Cyprus.<sup id="cite_ref-456"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-456">[447]</a></sup> Cooperation in the world's longest [submarine power cable](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Submarine_power_cable "Submarine power cable"), the [EuroAsia Interconnector](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/EuroAsia_Interconnector "EuroAsia Interconnector"), has strengthened [Cyprus–Israel relations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus%E2%80%93Israel_relations "Cyprus–Israel relations").<sup id="cite_ref-457"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-457">[448]</a></sup>

[Azerbaijan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan") is one of the few majority Muslim countries to develop strategic and economic [relations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan%E2%80%93Israel_relations "Azerbaijan–Israel relations") with Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-adalah_355-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-adalah-355">[346]</a></sup> Kazakhstan also has an economic and strategic partnership with Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-458"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-458">[449]</a></sup> India established full [diplomatic ties](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/India%E2%80%93Israel_relations "India–Israel relations") with Israel in 1992 and has fostered a strong military, technological and cultural partnership with the country since then.<sup id="cite_ref-459"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-459">[450]</a></sup> India is the largest customer of the [Israeli military equipment](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_military_equipment "Israeli military equipment") and Israel is the second-largest military partner of India after Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-460"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-460">[451]</a></sup> [Ethiopia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethiopia%E2%80%93Israel_relations "Ethiopia–Israel relations") is Israel's main ally in Africa due to common political, religious and security interests.<sup id="cite_ref-461"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-461">[452]</a></sup>

#### Foreign aid

Israel has a history of providing emergency [foreign aid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_foreign_aid "Israeli foreign aid") and humanitarian response to disasters across the world.<sup id="cite_ref-462"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-462">[453]</a></sup> In 1955 Israel began its foreign aid programme in Burma. The programme's focus subsequently shifted to Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Geldenhuys_463-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Geldenhuys-463">[454]</a></sup> Israel's humanitarian efforts officially began in 1957, with the establishment of [Mashav](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashav "Mashav"), the Israel's Agency for International Development Cooperation.<sup id="cite_ref-464"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-464">[455]</a></sup> In this early period, whilst Israel's aid represented only a small percentage of total aid to Africa, its programme was effective in creating goodwill; however, following the 1967 war relations soured.<sup id="cite_ref-Ismael_465-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Ismael-465">[456]</a></sup> Israel's foreign aid programme subsequently shifted its focus to Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-Geldenhuys_463-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Geldenhuys-463">[454]</a></sup> Since the late 1970s Israel's foreign aid has gradually decreased, although in recent years Israel has tried to reestablish aid to Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-466"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-466">[457]</a></sup> There are additional Israeli humanitarian and emergency response groups that work with the Israel government, including [IsraAid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/IsraAid "IsraAid"), a joint programme run by Israeli organizations and North American Jewish groups,<sup id="cite_ref-467"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-467">[458]</a></sup> [ZAKA](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/ZAKA "ZAKA"),<sup id="cite_ref-468"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-468">[459]</a></sup> The Fast Israeli Rescue and Search Team,<sup id="cite_ref-469"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-469">[460]</a></sup> Israeli Flying Aid,<sup id="cite_ref-470"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-470">[461]</a></sup> [Save a Child's Heart](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Save_a_Child%27s_Heart "Save a Child's Heart")<sup id="cite_ref-471"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-471">[462]</a></sup> and [Latet](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latet "Latet").<sup id="cite_ref-472"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-472">[463]</a></sup> Between 1985 and 2015, Israel sent 24 delegations of IDF search and rescue unit, the [Home Front Command](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_Front_Command "Home Front Command"), to 22 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-473"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-473">[464]</a></sup> Currently Israeli foreign aid [ranks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_development_aid_country_donors "List of development aid country donors") low among [OECD](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD") nations, spending less than 0.1% of its [GNI](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_national_income "Gross national income") on development assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-474"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-474">[465]</a></sup> The country ranked 38th in the 2018 [World Giving Index](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Giving_Index "World Giving Index").<sup id="cite_ref-475"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-475">[466]</a></sup>

### Military

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Southern_Lions._Squadron_116._I.jpg)

[F-35](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/F-35 "F-35") fighter jets of the [Israeli Air Force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force "Israeli Air Force")

The [Israel Defense Forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces "Israel Defense Forces") (IDF) is the sole military wing of the [Israeli security forces](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_security_forces "Israeli security forces") and is headed by its [Chief of General Staff](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_of_General_Staff_(Israel) "Chief of General Staff (Israel)"), the _Ramatkal_, subordinate to the [Cabinet](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_Israel "Cabinet of Israel"). The IDF consists of the [army](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/GOC_Army_Headquarters "GOC Army Headquarters"), [air force](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force "Israeli Air Force") and [navy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Navy "Israeli Navy"). It was founded during the [1948 Arab–Israeli War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War "1948 Arab–Israeli War") by consolidating paramilitary organizations—chiefly the [Haganah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haganah "Haganah").<sup id="cite_ref-476"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-476">[467]</a></sup> The IDF also draws upon the resources of the [Military Intelligence Directorate](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_Intelligence_Directorate_(Israel) "Military Intelligence Directorate (Israel)") (_Aman_).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenderson200397_477-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenderson200397-477">[468]</a></sup> The IDF have been involved in several [major wars](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_wars_involving_Israel "List of wars involving Israel") and border conflicts, making it one of the most battle-trained armed forces in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-478"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-478">[469]</a></sup>

Most Israelis are [conscripted](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription_in_Israel "Conscription in Israel") at age 18. Men serve two years and eight months and [women](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_the_Israel_Defense_Forces "Women in the Israel Defense Forces") two years.<sup id="cite_ref-479"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-479">[470]</a></sup> Following mandatory service, Israeli men join the reserve forces and usually do up to several weeks of [reserve duty](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reserve_duty_(Israel) "Reserve duty (Israel)") every year until their forties. Most women are exempt from reserve duty. [Arab citizens of Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_citizens_of_Israel "Arab citizens of Israel") (except the [Druze](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Druze_in_Israel "Druze in Israel")) and those engaged in full-time religious studies are [exempt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exemption_from_military_service_in_Israel "Exemption from military service in Israel"), although the [exemption of yeshiva students](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tal_committee "Tal committee") has been a source of contention.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStendel1997191–192_480-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStendel1997191%E2%80%93192-480">[471]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-481"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-481">[472]</a></sup> An alternative for those who receive exemptions on various grounds is _[Sherut Leumi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sherut_Leumi "Sherut Leumi")_, or national service, which involves a programme of service in social welfare frameworks.<sup id="cite_ref-482"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-482">[473]</a></sup> A small minority of Israeli Arabs also volunteer in the army.<sup id="cite_ref-483"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-483">[474]</a></sup> As a result of its conscription programme, the IDF maintains approximately 176,500 active troops and 465,000 reservists, giving Israel one of the world's highest [percentage of citizens with military training](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel "List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel").<sup id="cite_ref-IISS_military_484-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-IISS_military-484">[475]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:IDF_Air_Defense_fighters_during_Operation_Guardian_of_the_Walls,_May_2021._I.jpg)

[Iron Dome](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Dome "Iron Dome") is the world's first operational anti-[artillery rocket](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rocket_artillery "Rocket artillery") defense system.

The military relies heavily on high-tech [weapons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_equipment_of_Israel "Military equipment of Israel") systems [designed and manufactured in Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defense_industry_of_Israel "Defense industry of Israel") as well as some foreign imports. The [Arrow](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arrow_(Israeli_missile) "Arrow (Israeli missile)") missile is one of the world's few operational [anti-ballistic missile](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-ballistic_missile "Anti-ballistic missile") systems.<sup id="cite_ref-485"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-485">[476]</a></sup> The [Python](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Python_(missile) "Python (missile)") air-to-air missile series is often considered one of the most crucial weapons in its military history.<sup id="cite_ref-486"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-486">[477]</a></sup> Israel's [Spike](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spike_(missile) "Spike (missile)") missile is one of the most widely exported [anti-tank guided missiles](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-tank_guided_missile "Anti-tank guided missile") in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-487"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-487">[478]</a></sup> Israel's [Iron Dome](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Dome "Iron Dome") anti-missile air defense system gained worldwide acclaim after intercepting hundreds of [rockets fired by Palestinian militants](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_rocket_attacks_on_Israel "Palestinian rocket attacks on Israel") from the Gaza Strip.<sup id="cite_ref-Johnson_488-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Johnson-488">[479]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tory_489-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Tory-489">[480]</a></sup> Since the [Yom Kippur War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War "Yom Kippur War"), Israel has developed a network of [reconnaissance satellites](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconnaissance_satellites "Reconnaissance satellites").<sup id="cite_ref-490"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-490">[481]</a></sup> The _[Ofeq](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ofeq "Ofeq")_ programme has made Israel [one of seven countries](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_first_orbital_launches_by_country "Timeline of first orbital launches by country") capable of launching such satellites.<sup id="cite_ref-491"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-491">[482]</a></sup>

Israel is widely believed to [possess nuclear weapons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_and_Israel "Nuclear weapons and Israel")<sup id="cite_ref-492"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-492">[483]</a></sup> and per a 1993 report, chemical and biological [weapons of mass destruction](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction "Israel and weapons of mass destruction").<sup id="cite_ref-493"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-493">[484]</a></sup><sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated. (November 2021)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> Israel has not signed the [Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons "Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons")<sup id="cite_ref-494"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-494">[485]</a></sup> and maintains a [policy of deliberate ambiguity](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Policy_of_deliberate_ambiguity "Policy of deliberate ambiguity") toward its nuclear capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-495"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-495">[486]</a></sup> The Israeli Navy's [Dolphin submarines](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dolphin-class_submarine "Dolphin-class submarine") are believed to be armed with nuclear missiles offering [second-strike](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_strike "Second strike") capability.<sup id="cite_ref-496"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-496">[487]</a></sup> Since the [Gulf War](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War "Gulf War") in 1991, all homes in Israel are required to have a reinforced security room, [Merkhav Mugan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merkhav_Mugan "Merkhav Mugan"), impermeable to chemical and biological substances.<sup id="cite_ref-497"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-497">[488]</a></sup>

Since Israel's establishment, military expenditure constituted a significant portion of the country's [gross domestic product](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product"), with peak of 30.3% of GDP in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-498"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-498">[489]</a></sup> In 2021, Israel ranked 15th in the world [by total military expenditure](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures "List of countries by military expenditures"), with $24.3 billion, and 6th by defense spending as a percentage of GDP, with 5.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-499"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-499">[490]</a></sup> Since 1974, the United States has been a particularly notable contributor of [military aid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_military_relations#Military_aid_and_procurement "Israel–United States military relations").<sup id="cite_ref-500"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-500">[491]</a></sup> Under a [memorandum of understanding](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memorandum_of_understanding "Memorandum of understanding") signed in 2016, the U.S. is expected to provide the country with $3.8 billion per year, or around 20% of Israel's defense budget, from 2018 to 2028.<sup id="cite_ref-501"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-501">[492]</a></sup> Israel ranked 9th globally for [arms exports](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arms_industry "Arms industry") in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-502"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-502">[493]</a></sup> The majority of Israel's arms exports are unreported for security reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-503"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-503">[494]</a></sup> Israel is consistently rated low in the [Global Peace Index](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Peace_Index "Global Peace Index"), ranking 134th out of 163 nations in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-GPI_504-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-GPI-504">[495]</a></sup>

## Economy

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ayalon_Highway,_Tel_Aviv_(cropped).jpg)

The [Diamond Exchange District](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diamond_Exchange_District "Diamond Exchange District") in [Ramat Gan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramat_Gan "Ramat Gan")

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tel_Aviv_Stock_Exchange_-_New_Building_Lobby_1.jpg)

[Tel Aviv Stock Exchange](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv_Stock_Exchange "Tel Aviv Stock Exchange")

Israel is considered the most advanced country in [Western Asia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Asia "Western Asia") and the Middle East in economic and industrial development.<sup id="cite_ref-Chua_2003_219–220_505-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Chua_2003_219%E2%80%93220-505">[496]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-506"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-506">[497]</a></sup> As of October 2023, the IMF estimated Israel's GDP at 521.7 billion dollars and Israel's GDP per capita at 53.2 thousand ([ranking 13th worldwide](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita "List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita")).<sup id="cite_ref-507"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-507">[498]</a></sup> It is the third richest country in Asia [by nominal per capita](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita "List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita") income.<sup id="cite_ref-508"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-508">[499]</a></sup> Israel has the highest average [wealth per adult](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_wealth_per_adult "List of countries by wealth per adult") in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-CS_2019-1_509-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-CS_2019-1-509">[500]</a></sup>_[The Economist](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Economist "The Economist")_ ranked Israel as the 4th most successful economy among the developed countries for 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-510"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-510">[501]</a></sup> It has the [most billionaires](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_billionaires "List of countries by number of billionaires") in the Middle East, and the 18th most in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-511"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-511">[502]</a></sup> In recent years Israel had one of the highest growth rates in the developed world.<sup id="cite_ref-512"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-512">[503]</a></sup> In 2010, it joined the [OECD](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD").<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_48-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-OECD-48">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-513"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-513">[504]</a></sup> The country is ranked 20th in the [World Economic Forum](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Economic_Forum "World Economic Forum")'s _[Global Competitiveness Report](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report "Global Competitiveness Report")_<sup id="cite_ref-rank_2019_514-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-rank_2019-514">[505]</a></sup> and 35th on the [World Bank](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank "World Bank")'s [_Ease of Doing Business_ index](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index "Ease of doing business index").<sup id="cite_ref-515"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-515">[506]</a></sup> Israel was also ranked 5th in the world by share of people in high-skilled employment.<sup id="cite_ref-516"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-516">[507]</a></sup> Israeli economic data covers the economic territory of Israel, including the Golan Heights, East Jerusalem and Israeli settlements in the West Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOECD2011_368-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOECD2011-368">[359]</a></sup>

Despite limited natural resources, intensive development of the [agricultural](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agriculture_in_Israel "Agriculture in Israel") and industrial sectors over the past decades has made Israel largely self-sufficient in food production, apart from grains and beef. Imports to Israel, totaling $96.5 billion in 2020, include raw materials, military equipment, investment goods, rough diamonds, fuels, grain, and consumer goods.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_314-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cia-314">[305]</a></sup> Leading exports include machinery, equipment, software, [cut diamonds](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diamond_industry_in_Israel "Diamond industry in Israel"), agricultural products, chemicals, textiles, and apparel; in 2020, Israeli exports reached $114 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_314-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cia-314">[305]</a></sup> The [Bank of Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bank_of_Israel "Bank of Israel") holds $201 billion of [foreign-exchange reserves](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign-exchange_reserves "Foreign-exchange reserves"), the 17th highest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_314-5"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cia-314">[305]</a></sup> Since the 1970s, Israel has received [military aid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_military_relations "Israel–United States military relations") from the United States, as well as economic assistance in the form of [loan guarantees](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loan_guarantee "Loan guarantee"), which account for roughly half of Israel's [external debt](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/External_debt "External debt"). Israel has [one of the lowest](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_external_debt "List of countries by external debt") external debts in the developed world, and is a lender in terms of net external debt ([assets vs. liabilities abroad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Net_international_investment_position "Net international investment position")), which in 2015 stood at a surplus of $69 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-517"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-517">[508]</a></sup>

Israel has the second-largest number of [startup companies](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Startup_company "Startup company") after the United States,<sup id="cite_ref-518"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-518">[509]</a></sup> and the third-largest number of [NASDAQ-listed companies](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Israeli_companies_quoted_on_the_Nasdaq "List of Israeli companies quoted on the Nasdaq").<sup id="cite_ref-519"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-519">[510]</a></sup> It is the world leader for number of start-ups per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-520"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-520">[511]</a></sup> Israel has been dubbed the "[Start-Up Nation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Start-up_Nation "Start-up Nation")".<sup id="cite_ref-521"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-521">[512]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-522"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-522">[513]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-523"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-523">[514]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-524"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-524">[515]</a></sup> [Intel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intel "Intel")<sup id="cite_ref-525"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-525">[516]</a></sup> and [Microsoft](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft "Microsoft")<sup id="cite_ref-526"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-526">[517]</a></sup> built their first overseas [research and development](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Research_and_development "Research and development") facilities in Israel, and other high-tech multinational corporations have opened [research and development centres in the country](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_multinational_companies_with_research_and_development_centres_in_Israel "List of multinational companies with research and development centres in Israel").

The days which are allocated to working times in Israel are Sunday through Thursday (for a five-day [workweek](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workweek "Workweek")), or Friday (for a six-day workweek). In observance of _[Shabbat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shabbat "Shabbat")_, in places where Friday is a work day and the majority of population is Jewish, Friday is a "short day". Several proposals have been raised to adjust the work week with the majority of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-527"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-527">[518]</a></sup>

### Science and technology

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Matam_hi-tech_park_(Haifa).jpg)

[Matam](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matam,_Haifa "Matam, Haifa") high-tech park in Haifa

Israel's development of cutting-edge technologies in software, communications and the life sciences have [evoked comparisons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicon_Wadi "Silicon Wadi") with [Silicon Valley](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicon_Valley "Silicon Valley").<sup id="cite_ref-528"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-528">[519]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-529"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-529">[520]</a></sup> Israel is first in the world in [expenditure on research and development](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_research_and_development_spending "List of countries by research and development spending") as a percentage of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_R&amp;D_530-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-OECD_R&amp;D-530">[521]</a></sup> It is ranked 14th in the [Global Innovation Index](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index "Global Innovation Index") in 2023,<sup id="cite_ref-531"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-531">[522]</a></sup> and fifth in the 2019 [Bloomberg Innovation Index](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bloomberg_Innovation_Index "Bloomberg Innovation Index").<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_innovation_532-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Bloomberg_innovation-532">[523]</a></sup> Israel has 140 scientists, technicians, and engineers per 10,000 employees, the highest number in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-533"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-533">[524]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-534"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-534">[525]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-535"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-535">[526]</a></sup> Israel has produced six [Nobel Prize-winning](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Israeli_Nobel_laureates "List of Israeli Nobel laureates") scientists since 2004<sup id="cite_ref-nobel_536-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-nobel-536">[527]</a></sup> and has been frequently ranked as one of the countries with the highest ratios of [scientific papers](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_papers "Scientific papers") per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-537"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-537">[528]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-538"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-538">[529]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-539"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-539">[530]</a></sup> [Israeli universities](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Israeli_universities_and_colleges "List of Israeli universities and colleges") are ranked among the top 50 world universities in computer science ([Technion](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technion "Technion") and [Tel Aviv University](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tel_Aviv_University "Tel Aviv University")), mathematics ([Hebrew University of Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_University_of_Jerusalem "Hebrew University of Jerusalem")) and chemistry ([Weizmann Institute of Science](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weizmann_Institute_of_Science "Weizmann Institute of Science")).<sup id="cite_ref-ARWU_540-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-ARWU-540">[531]</a></sup>

In 2012, Israel was ranked ninth in the world by the Futron's [Space Competitiveness Index](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Competitiveness_Index "Space Competitiveness Index").<sup id="cite_ref-541"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-541">[532]</a></sup> The [Israel Space Agency](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Space_Agency "Israel Space Agency") coordinates all Israeli space research programmes with scientific and commercial goals, and have designed and built at least 13 commercial, research and spy satellites.<sup id="cite_ref-542"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-542">[533]</a></sup> Some of Israel's satellites are ranked among the world's most advanced space systems.<sup id="cite_ref-543"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-543">[534]</a></sup> [Shavit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shavit_2 "Shavit 2") is a space [launch vehicle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Launch_vehicle "Launch vehicle") produced by Israel to launch small [satellites](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satellite "Satellite") into [low Earth orbit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit "Low Earth orbit").<sup id="cite_ref-544"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-544">[535]</a></sup> It was first launched in 1988, making Israel the [eighth nation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_first_orbital_launches_by_country "Timeline of first orbital launches by country") to have a space launch capability. In 2003, [Ilan Ramon](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilan_Ramon "Ilan Ramon") became Israel's first astronaut, serving on the [fatal mission](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster "Space Shuttle Columbia disaster") of [Space Shuttle _Columbia_](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia "Space Shuttle Columbia").<sup id="cite_ref-545"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-545">[536]</a></sup>

The ongoing [water shortage](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Israel "Water supply and sanitation in Israel") has spurred innovation in [water conservation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_conservation "Water conservation") techniques, and a substantial [agricultural modernization](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agricultural_research_in_Israel "Agricultural research in Israel"), [drip irrigation](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drip_irrigation "Drip irrigation"), was [invented in Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Israeli_inventions_and_discoveries "List of Israeli inventions and discoveries"). Israel is also at the technological forefront of [desalination](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desalination "Desalination") and [water recycling](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_recycling "Water recycling"). The [Sorek desalination plant](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorek_desalination_plant "Sorek desalination plant") is the largest seawater [reverse osmosis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reverse_osmosis "Reverse osmosis") desalination facility in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-546"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-546">[537]</a></sup> By 2014, Israel's desalination programmes provided roughly 35% of Israel's drinking water and it is expected to supply 70% by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-547"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-547">[538]</a></sup> As of 2015, over 50 percent of the water for Israeli households, agriculture and industry is artificially produced.<sup id="cite_ref-Kershner_548-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Kershner-548">[539]</a></sup> In 2011, Israel's [water technology industry](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_industry "Water industry") was worth around $2 billion a year with annual exports of products and services in the tens of millions of dollars. As a result of innovations in reverse osmosis technology, Israel is set to become a net [exporter of water](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_export "Water export").<sup id="cite_ref-549"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-549">[540]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Solar_dish_at_Ben-Gurion_National_Solar_Energy_Center_in_Israel.jpg)

The world's largest [solar parabolic dish](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parabolic_reflector "Parabolic reflector") at the [Ben-Gurion National Solar Energy Center](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben-Gurion_National_Solar_Energy_Center "Ben-Gurion National Solar Energy Center")<sup id="cite_ref-Register_550-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Register-550">[541]</a></sup>

Israel has embraced [solar energy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solar_power_in_Israel "Solar power in Israel"); its engineers are on the cutting edge of solar energy technology<sup id="cite_ref-NPR_551-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-NPR-551">[542]</a></sup> and its solar companies work on projects around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-CBC_552-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-CBC-552">[543]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BW_553-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-BW-553">[544]</a></sup> Over 90% of Israeli homes use solar energy for hot water, the highest per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-Solar_energy_336-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Solar_energy-336">[327]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Environment_California_SWH_554-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Environment_California_SWH-554">[545]</a></sup> According to government figures, the country saves 8% of its electricity consumption per year because of its solar energy use in heating.<sup id="cite_ref-555"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-555">[546]</a></sup> The high annual incident [solar irradiance](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irradiance "Irradiance") at its geographic [latitude](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latitude "Latitude") creates ideal conditions for what is an internationally renowned solar research and development industry in the [Negev Desert](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev_Desert "Negev Desert").<sup id="cite_ref-NPR_551-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-NPR-551">[542]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CBC_552-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-CBC-552">[543]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BW_553-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-BW-553">[544]</a></sup> Israel had a modern [electric car infrastructure](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electric_vehicle_network "Electric vehicle network") involving a countrywide network of [charging stations](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charging_station "Charging station").<sup id="cite_ref-556"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-556">[547]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-557"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-557">[548]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-558"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-558">[549]</a></sup> However, Israel's electric car company [Better Place](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Better_Place_(company) "Better Place (company)") shut down in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-559"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-559">[550]</a></sup>

### Energy

Israel began producing natural gas from its own offshore gas fields in 2004. In 2009, a [natural gas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas_in_Israel "Natural gas in Israel") reserve, [Tamar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamar_gas_field "Tamar gas field"), was found near the coast of Israel. A second reserve, [Leviathan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leviathan_gas_field "Leviathan gas field"), was discovered in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-560"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-560">[551]</a></sup> The natural gas reserves in these two fields could make Israel energy-secure for more than 50 years. In 2013, Israel began commercial production of natural gas from the Tamar field. As of 2014, Israel produced over 7.5 billion cubic meters (bcm) of [natural gas](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas "Natural gas") a year.<sup id="cite_ref-561"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-561">[552]</a></sup> Israel had 199 billion bcm of proven reserves of natural gas as of 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-562"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-562">[553]</a></sup> The Leviathan gas field started production in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-563"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-563">[554]</a></sup>

[Ketura Sun](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ketura_Sun "Ketura Sun") is Israel's first commercial solar field. Built in 2011 by the [Arava Power Company](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arava_Power_Company "Arava Power Company"), the field consists of 18,500 [photovoltaic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Photovoltaics "Photovoltaics") panels made by [Suntech](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suntech_Power "Suntech Power"), which will produce about 9 [gigawatt-hours](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gigawatt-hour "Gigawatt-hour") (GWh) of electricity per year.<sup id="cite_ref-564"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-564">[555]</a></sup> In the next twenty years, the field will spare the production of some 125,000 metric tons of carbon dioxide.<sup id="cite_ref-565"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-565">[556]</a></sup>

### Transport

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:4X-ECC_LLBG_09-05-2014b.jpg)

[Ben Gurion International Airport](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Gurion_International_Airport "Ben Gurion International Airport")

Israel has 19,224 kilometres (11,945 mi) of paved [roads](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roads_in_Israel "Roads in Israel")<sup id="cite_ref-566"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-566">[557]</a></sup> and 3 million motor vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-vehicles_567-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-vehicles-567">[558]</a></sup> The [number of motor vehicles per 1,000 persons](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_vehicles_per_capita "List of countries by vehicles per capita") is 365, relatively low among developed countries.<sup id="cite_ref-vehicles_567-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-vehicles-567">[558]</a></sup> Israel has 5,715 buses on scheduled routes,<sup id="cite_ref-568"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-568">[559]</a></sup> operated by several carriers, the largest and oldest of which is [Egged](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egged_(company) "Egged (company)"), serving most of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-569"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-569">[560]</a></sup> [Railways](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Israel "Rail transport in Israel") stretch across 1,277 kilometres (793 mi) and are operated by government-owned [Israel Railways](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel_Railways "Israel Railways").<sup id="cite_ref-cbs_rails_570-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cbs_rails-570">[561]</a></sup> Following major investments beginning in the early to mid-1990s, the number of train passengers per year has grown from 2.5 million in 1990, to 53 million in 2015; railways transport 7.5 million tons of cargo per year.<sup id="cite_ref-cbs_rails_570-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-cbs_rails-570">[561]</a></sup>

Israel is served by three international [airports](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Israel "List of airports in Israel"): [Ben Gurion Airport](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Gurion_Airport "Ben Gurion Airport"), the country's main hub for international air travel; [Ramon Airport](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramon_Airport "Ramon Airport"); and [Haifa Airport](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haifa_Airport "Haifa Airport"). Ben Gurion, Israel's largest airport, handled over 15 million passengers in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-571"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-571">[562]</a></sup> The country has three main ports: the [Port of Haifa](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_of_Haifa "Port of Haifa"), the country's oldest and largest, on the [Mediterranean](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean "Mediterranean") coast, [Ashdod Port](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashdod_Port "Ashdod Port"); and the smaller [Port of Eilat](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_of_Eilat "Port of Eilat") on the [Red Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Sea "Red Sea").

### Tourism

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ein_Bokek_-_Dead_Sea2.jpg)

[Ein Bokek](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ein_Bokek "Ein Bokek") resort on the shore of the [Dead Sea](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dead_Sea "Dead Sea")

Tourism, especially [religious tourism](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_tourism "Religious tourism"), is an important industry in Israel, with the country's [beaches](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_beaches_in_Israel "List of beaches in Israel"), [archaeological](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaeology_of_Israel "Archaeology of Israel"), other [historical](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Israel "List of World Heritage Sites in Israel") and [biblical](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_biblical_places "List of biblical places") sites, and unique geography also drawing tourists. Israel's security problems have taken their toll on the industry, but the number of tourists is on the rebound.<sup id="cite_ref-572"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-572">[563]</a></sup> In 2017, a record 3.6 million tourists visited Israel, yielding a 25 percent growth since 2016 and contributed NIS 20 billion to the Israeli economy.<sup id="cite_ref-573"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-573">[564]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-574"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-574">[565]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-575"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-575">[566]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-576"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-576">[567]</a></sup>

### Real estate

Housing prices in Israel are listed in the top third of all countries,<sup id="cite_ref-577"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-577">[568]</a></sup> with an average of 150 salaries required to buy an apartment.<sup id="cite_ref-578"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-578">[569]</a></sup> As of 2022, there are about 2.7 million properties in Israel, with an annual increase of over 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-579"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-579">[570]</a></sup> However, the demand for housing exceeds supply, with a shortage of about 200,000 apartments as of 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-580"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-580">[571]</a></sup> As a result, by 2021 housing prices rose by 5.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-581"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-581">[572]</a></sup> In 2021, Israelis took a record of NIS 116.1 billion in mortgages, an increase of 50% from 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-582"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-582">[573]</a></sup>

## Demographics

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Aliyah_1948-2015.png)

[Immigration to Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_to_Israel "Immigration to Israel") in the years 1948–2015. The two peaks were in 1949 and 1990

Israel has the largest Jewish population in the world and is the only country where Jews are the majority.<sup id="cite_ref-583"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-583">[574]</a></sup> As of 31 December 2022, Israel's population was an estimated 9,656,000. In 2022, the government recorded 73.6% of the population as [Jews](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Jews "Israeli Jews"), 21.1% as [Arabs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_citizens_of_Israel "Arab citizens of Israel"), and 5.3% as "Others" (non-Arab Christians and people who have no religion listed).<sup id="cite_ref-population_stat2022_15-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-population_stat2022-15">[12]</a></sup> Over the last decade, large numbers of migrant workers from Romania, Thailand, China, Africa, and South America have settled in Israel. Exact figures are unknown, as many of them are living in the country illegally,<sup id="cite_ref-584"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-584">[575]</a></sup> but estimates run from 166,000 to 203,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Adriana_Kemp_585-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Adriana_Kemp-585">[576]</a></sup> By June 2012, approximately 60,000 [African migrants](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illegal_immigration_from_Africa_to_Israel "Illegal immigration from Africa to Israel") had entered Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-586"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-586">[577]</a></sup> About 93% of Israelis live in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-587"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-587">[578]</a></sup> 90% of [Palestinian Israelis](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_citizens_of_Israel "Palestinian citizens of Israel") reside in 139 densely populated towns and villages concentrated in the Galilee, [Triangle](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triangle_(Israel) "Triangle (Israel)") and [Negev](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negev "Negev") regions, with the remaining 10% in [mixed cities](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixed_cities "Mixed cities") and neighbourhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-588"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-588">[579]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-589"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-589">[580]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-590"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-590">[581]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-591"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-591">[582]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-592"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-592">[583]</a></sup> The [OECD](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD") in 2016 estimated the average [life expectancy](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_expectancy "Life expectancy") at 82.5 years, the [6th-highest in the world](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy "List of countries by life expectancy").<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_life_expec_593-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-OECD_life_expec-593">[584]</a></sup> Israeli Arab life expectancy lags by 3 to 4 years<sup id="cite_ref-594"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-594">[585]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-595"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-595">[586]</a></sup> and is higher than in most Arab and Muslim countries.<sup id="cite_ref-596"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-596">[587]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-597"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-597">[588]</a></sup> Retention of Israel's population since 1948 is about even or greater, when compared to other countries with mass immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-598"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-598">[589]</a></sup> Jewish emigration from Israel (called _[yerida](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yerida "Yerida")_), primarily to the United States and Canada, is described by demographers as modest,<sup id="cite_ref-599"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-599">[590]</a></sup> but is often cited by Israeli government ministries as a major threat to Israel's future.<sup id="cite_ref-600"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-600">[591]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-601"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-601">[592]</a></sup>

Approximately 80% of [Israeli Jews](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_Jews "Israeli Jews") are [born in Israel](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabra_(person) "Sabra (person)"), 14% are immigrants from Europe and the Americas, and 6% are immigrants from Asia and Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-602"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-602">[593]</a></sup> Jews from Europe and the former [Soviet Union](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") and their descendants born in Israel, including [Ashkenazi Jews](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews "Ashkenazi Jews"), constitute approximately 44% of Jewish Israelis. [Jews from Arab and Muslim countries](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_exodus_from_Arab_and_Muslim_countries "Jewish exodus from Arab and Muslim countries") and their descendants, including both [Mizrahi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mizrahi_Jews "Mizrahi Jews") and [Sephardi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sephardi_Jews "Sephardi Jews") Jews,<sup id="cite_ref-603"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-603">[594]</a></sup> form most of the rest of the Jewish population.<sup id="cite_ref-604"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-604">[595]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-605"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-605">[596]</a></sup> Jewish intermarriage rates run at over 35% and recent studies suggest that the percentage of Israelis descended from both Sephardi and Ashkenazi Jews increases by 0.5 percent yearly, with over 25% of schoolchildren now originating from both.<sup id="cite_ref-606"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-606">[597]</a></sup> Around 4% of Israelis (300,000), ethnically defined as "others", are [Russian descendants](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990s_Post-Soviet_aliyah "1990s Post-Soviet aliyah") of Jewish origin or family who are not Jewish according to rabbinical law, but were eligible for citizenship under the Law of Return.<sup id="cite_ref-607"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-607">[598]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Israel_people_608-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-Israel_people-608">[599]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-609"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel#cite_note-609">[600]</a></sup>
